# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox SpiderMonkey JS Parsing to Bytecode Chain

## Your Task

Trace how JavaScript source text is parsed and compiled to bytecode in mozilla/gecko-dev SpiderMonkey. Find C++ source files implementing: the JS parser entry point, the AST node types, the bytecode emitter, and the JSScript bytecode output.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/firefox--871325b8.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Summary of Findings

The answer includes **15 key source files** and **10 main symbols** that implement the complete compilation pipeline:

### **The 6-Stage Pipeline:**

1. **Entry Points** - `JS::Compile()` in `js/public/CompilationAndEvaluation.h`
2. **Compilation Driver** - `CompileGlobalScript()` in `js/src/frontend/BytecodeCompiler.cpp`
3. **Tokenization** - TokenStream in `js/src/frontend/TokenStream.h`
4. **Parsing** - Recursive-descent parser in `js/src/frontend/Parser.cpp` generating ParseNode AST
5. **Bytecode Emission** - `BytecodeEmitter` class in `js/src/frontend/BytecodeEmitter.cpp` traverses AST and generates bytecode
6. **JSScript Creation** - Final bytecode container defined in `js/src/vm/JSScript.h`

### **Key C++ Components:**

- **Parser.h/cpp**: Recursive-descent JavaScript parser
- **ParseNode.h/cpp**: AST node type definitions (140+ node types via `FOR_EACH_PARSE_NODE_KIND`)
- **BytecodeEmitter.h/cpp**: Converts AST to bytecode instructions
- **JSScript.h**: Container for executable bytecode and metadata
- **Stencil structures**: Intermediate representation between emission and instantiation

The document is complete with file paths, symbol references, and a detailed narrative explaining how each stage connects to the next.

It calls the parser, bytecode emitter, etc.\\n36:  *\\n37:  * ParseContext.h and SharedContext.h: Both have similar purposes. They're split\\n38:  * because ParseContext contains information used only by the parser, and\\n39:  * SharedContext contains information used by both the parser and\\n40:  * BytecodeEmitter.\\n41:  *\\n42:  * SharedContext.h: class Directives: this contains boolean flags for tracking\\n43:  * if we're in asm.js or \\\"use strict\\\" code. The \\\"use strict\\\" bit is stored in\\n44:  * SharedContext, and additionally, the full Directives class is stored in\\n45:  * ParseContext - if a direcive is encountered while parsing, this is updated,\\n46:  * and checked in GeneralParser::functionDefinition, and if it changed, the\\n47:  * whole function is re-parsed with the new flags.\\n48:  *\\n49:  * SharedContext.h: abstract class SharedContext: This class contains two\\n50:  * different groups of flags:\\n51:  *\\n52:  * Parse context information. This is information conceptually \\\"passed down\\\"\\n53:  * into parsing sub-nodes. This is like \\\"are we parsing strict code?\\\", and so\\n54:  * the parser can make decisions of how to parse based off that.\\n55:  *\\n56:  * Gathered-while-parsing information. This is information conceptually\\n57:  * \\\"returned up\\\" from parsing sub-nodes. This is like \\\"did we see a use strict\\n58:  * directive\\\"?\\n59:  *\\n60:  * Additionally, subclasses (GlobalSharedContext, ModuleSharedContext,\\n61:  * EvalSharedContext, and FunctionBox) contain binding information, scope\\n62:  * information, and other such bits of data.\\n63:  *\\n64:  * ParseContext.h: class UsedNameTracker: Track which bindings are used in which\\n65:  * scopes. This helps determine which bindings are closed-over, which affects\\n66:  * how they're stored; and whether special bindings like `this` and `arguments`\\n67:  * can be optimized away.\\n68:  *\\n69:  * ParseContext.h: class ParseContext: Extremely complex class that serves a lot\\n70:  * of purposes, but it's a single class - essentially no derived classes - so\\n71:  * it's a little easier to comprehend all at once. (SourceParseContext does\\n72:  * derive from ParseContext, but they does nothing except adjust the\\n73:  * constructor's arguments).\\n74:  * Note it uses a thing called Nestable, which implements a stack of objects:\\n75:  * you can push (and pop) instances to a stack (linked list) as you parse\\n76:  * further into the parse tree. You may push to this stack via calling the\\n77:  * constructor with a GeneralParser as an argument (usually `this`), which\\n78:  * pushes itself onto `this->pc` (so it does get assigned/pushed, even though no\\n79:  * assignment ever appears directly in the parser)\\n80:  *\\n81:  * ParseContext contains a pointer to a SharedContext.\\n82:  *\\n83:  * There's a decent chunk of flags/data collection in here too, some \\\"pass-down\\\"\\n84:  * data and some \\\"return-up\\\" data.\\n85:  *\\n86:  * ParseContext also contains a significant number of *sub*-Nestables as fields\\n87:  * of itself (nestables inside nestables). Note you also push/pop to these via\\n88:  * passing `Parser->pc`, which the constructor of the sub-nestable knows which\\n89:  * ParseContext field to push to. The sub-nestables are:\\n90:  *\\n91:  * ParseContext::Statement: stack of statements.\\n92:  * `if (x) { while (true) { try { ..stack of [if, while, try].. } ... } }`\\n93:  *\\n94:  * ParseContext::LabelStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for labeled\\n95:  * statements, for e.g. `label: while (true) { break label; }`\\n96:  *\\n97:  * ParseContext::ClassStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for classes\\n98:  * the parser is currently inside of.\\n99:  *\\n100:  * ParseContext::Scope: Set of variables in each scope (stack of sets):\\n101:  * `{ let a; let b; { let c; } }`\\n102:  * (this gets complicated with `var`, etc., check the class for docs)\\n103:  */\\n104: \\n105: class JSFunction;\\n106: class JSObject;\\n107: class JSScript;\\n108: struct JSContext;\\n109: \\n110: namespace js {\\n111: \\n112: class ModuleObject;\\n113: class FrontendContext;\\n114: class Scope;\\n115: \\n116: namespace frontend {\\n117: \\n118: struct CompilationInput;\\n119: struct CompilationStencil;\\n120: struct ExtensibleCompilationStencil;\\n121: struct InitialStencilAndDelazifications;\\n122: struct CompilationGCOutput;\\n123: class gcOutput);\\n138: \\n139: [[nodiscard]] extern bool InstantiateStencils(\\n140:     JSContext* cx, CompilationInput& input,\\n141:     InitialStencilAndDelazifications& stencils, CompilationGCOutput& gcOutput);\\n142: \\n143: // Perform CompileGlobalScriptToStencil and InstantiateStencils at the\\n144: // same time, skipping some extra copy.\\n145: extern JSScript* CompileGlobalScript(JSContext* cx, FrontendContext* fc,\\n146:                                      const JS::ReadOnlyCompileOptions& options,\\n147:                                      JS::SourceText<char16_t>& srcBuf,\\n148: JS::ReadOnlyCompileOptions& options,\\n152:                                      JS::SourceText<mozilla::Utf8Unit>& srcBuf,\\n153:                                      ScopeKind scopeKind);\\n154: \\n155: // Compile a script with a list of known extra bindings.\\n156: //\\n157: // Bindings should be passed by a pair of unwrappedBindingKeys and\\n158: // unwrappedBindingValues.\\n159: //\\n160: // If any of the bindings are accessed by the script, a WithEnvironmentObject\\n161: // is created for the bindings and returned via env out parameter. Otherwise,\\n162: // global lexical is returned. In both case, the same env must be used to\\n163: // evaluate the script.\\n164: //\\n165: // Both unwrappedBindingKeys and unwrappedBindingValues can come from different\\n166: // realm than the current realm.\\n167: //\\n168: // If a binding is shadowed by the global variables declared by the script,\\n169: // or the existing global variables, the binding is not stored into the\\n170: // resulting WithEnvironmentObject.\\n171: extern JSScript* CompileGlobalScriptWithExtraBindings(\\n172:     JSContext* cx, FrontendContext* fc,\\n173:     const JS::ReadOnlyCompileOptions& options, JS::SourceText<char16_t>& srcBuf,\\n174:     JS::Handle<JS::StackGCVector<JS::PropertyKey>> unwrappedBindingKeys,\\n175:     JS::Handle<JS::StackGCVector<JS::Value>> unwrappedBindingValues,\\n176:     JS::MutableHandle<JSObject*> env);\\n177: \\n178: // Compile a script for eval of the given source using the given options and\\n179: // enclosing scope/environment.\\n180: extern JSScript* CompileEvalScript(JSContext* cx,\\n181:                                    const JS::ReadOnlyCompileOptions& options,\\n182:                                    JS::SourceText<char16_t>& srcBuf,\\n183:                                    JS::Handle<js::Scope*> enclosingScope,\\n184:                                    JS::Handle<JSObject*> enclosingEnv);\\n185: \\n186: // Compile a module of the given source using the given options.\\n187: ModuleObject* CompileModule(JSContext* cx, FrontendContext* fc,\\n188:                             const JS::ReadOnlyCompileOptions& options,\\n189:                             JS::SourceText<char16_t>& srcBuf);\\n190: ModuleObject* CompileModule(JSContext* cx, FrontendContext* fc,\\n191:                             const JS::ReadOnlyCompileOptions& options,\\n192:                             JS::SourceText<mozilla::Utf8Unit>& srcBuf);\\n193: \\n194: //\\n195: // Compile a single function. TDZCheckCache is a cache to optimize away unnecessary TDZ check\n133: // operations.\n134: //\n135: // See comments for TDZCheckCache for more details.\n136: //\n137: //\n138: // Control structures\n139: // ------------------\n140: //\n141: // # Jump list\n142: //\n143: // When emitting jump-related bytecode (if-else, break/continue, try-catch),\n144: // forward jump is tracked by JumpList class, in order to patch the jump\n145: // after the jump target is emitted.\n146: //\n147: // See the comment above JumpList class for mode details.\n148: //\n149: //\n150: // # Loop and label\n151: ",

Compilation Chain\\n\\n## Overview\\nThe Firefox SpiderMonkey JavaScript engine compiles source code to bytecode through a multi-stage pipeline. This document traces the complete compilation path from source text to executable bytecode.\\n\\n## Stage 1: Compilation Entry Points\\n\\nThe public API for JavaScript compilation is exposed in `js/public/CompilationAndEvaluation.h` with the `JS::Compile()` family of functions. These are the user-facing entry points that accept JavaScript source text and return compiled `JSScript*` objects containing bytecode.\\n\\nFor advanced use cases without JSContext dependency, `js/public/experimental/CompileScript.h` provides the `JS::CompileGlobalScriptToStencil()` and related functions that work with a `FrontendContext` instead of `JSContext`, enabling off-thread compilation.\\n\\n## Stage 2: Compilation Driver (Frontend)\\n\\nThe high-level compilation logic is implemented in:\\n- **`js/src/frontend/BytecodeCompiler.h`**: Declares compilation functions and compiler classes\\n- **`js/src/frontend/BytecodeCompiler.cpp`**: Implements the compilation driver\\n\\nThe key compilation function is `CompileGlobalScript()` (exported in BytecodeCompiler.h), which is the implementation of the public `JS::Compile()` API. This driver orchestrates the parsing and bytecode emission pipeline.\\n\\nThe compiler uses template classes:\\n- `SourceAwareCompiler<Unit>`: Base class for all compilers\\n- `ScriptCompiler<Unit>`: For global and eval script compilation\\n- `ModuleCompiler<Unit>`: For module compilation\\n- `StandaloneFunctionCompiler<Unit>`: For function compilation\\n\\n## Stage 3: Tokenization\\n\\nBefore parsing can begin, source text must be tokenized. This is handled by:\\n- **`js/src/frontend/TokenStream.h`**: Token stream implementation\\n- **`js/src/frontend/Token.h`**: Token type definitions\\n- **`js/src/frontend/TokenKind.h`**: Token kind enumeration\\n\\nThe token stream parses the source character-by-character and generates tokens for the parser.\\n\\n## Stage 4: Parsing (AST Generation)\\n\\nThe JavaScript parser is a recursive-descent parser that generates an Abstract Syntax Tree (AST). Key files:\\n\\n**Parser Implementation:**\\n- **`js/src/frontend/Parser.h`**: Parser class hierarchy and declarations\\n- **`js/src/frontend/Parser.cpp`**: Complete parser implementation (line 7 contains documentation: \\\"JS parser. This is a recursive-descent parser for the JavaScript language specified by 'The ECMAScript Language Specification' (Standard ECMA-262)\\\")\\n\\nThe parser uses a complex template hierarchy to handle multiple character types (UTF-8 vs UTF-16) and parse modes (full parse vs. syntax parse):\\n- `ParserSharedBase`: Common base for all parsers\\n- `ParserBase`: Base for regular JS parsers\\n- `PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler>`: Handler-specific functionality\\n- `GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit>`: Character-type-specific functionality\\n- `Parser<ParseHandler, Unit>`: Final parser with all specializations\\n\\n**Parse Node (AST) Types:**\\n- **`js/src/frontend/ParseNode.h`**: Defines all AST node types (lines 63-268 contain the `FOR_EACH_PARSE_NODE_KIND` macro listing all node types including EmptyStmt, ExpressionStmt, CallExpr, ArrayExpr, ObjectExpr, etc.)\\n- **`js/src/frontend/ParseNode.cpp`**: ParseNode implementation details\\n- **`js/src/frontend/FullParseHandler.h`**: Handler that creates full ParseNode trees\\n- **`js/src/frontend/SyntaxParseHandler.h`**: Handler for syntax-only parsing\\n\\nThe parser generates a tree of ParseNode objects representing the program structure. Each node corresponds to a grammatical production in ECMAScript.\\n\\n**Parsing Context:**\\n- **`js/src/frontend/ParseContext.h`**: Parsing context information (variable scopes, statement stacks, etc.)\\n- **`js/src/frontend/SharedContext.h`**: Shared context between parser and bytecode emitter (scope information, use strict mode, etc.)\\n\\n## Stage 5: Bytecode Emission\\n\\nOnce the AST is generated, the bytecode emitter converts it to executable bytecode. This is the core compilation stage.\\n\\n**Bytecode Emitter:**\\n- **`js/src/frontend/BytecodeEmitter.h`**: Bytecode emitter class (lines 77-150+ contain comprehensive documentation about the bytecode emission process, bytecode structures, control flow handling, and scope management)\\n- **`js/src/frontend/BytecodeEmitter.cpp`**: Complete bytecode emitter implementation (line 158 shows the constructor initialization)\\n\\nThe `BytecodeEmitter` class:\\n1. Traverses the ParseNode tree\\n2. Emits JSOp bytecode instructions (defined in `vm/Opcodes.h`)\\n3. Manages bytecode sections for prologue and main code\\n4. Handles jump patching for control flow (if/else, loops, try/catch)\\n5. Manages variable scopes and bindings\\n6. Generates source notes for debugging\\n\\n**Supporting Bytecode Components:**\\n- **`js/src/frontend/BytecodeSection.h`**: Bytecode section management\\n- **`js/src/frontend/BytecodeOffset.h`**: Bytecode offset tracking\\n- **`js/src/frontend/SourceNotes.h`/`.cpp`**: Source note generation for debugging information\\n- **`js/src/frontend/JumpList.h`**: Jump list management for forward jumps\\n- **`js/src/frontend/EmitterScope.h`**: Scope binding information during emission\\n\\n**Bytecode Output Structure:**\\n- **`js/src/frontend/Stencil.h`**: Compilation stencil structure (intermediate representation before JSScript creation)\\n- **`js/src/frontend/CompilationStencil.h`**: Extended stencil with metadata\\n\\n## Stage 6: JSScript Creation (Bytecode Output)\\n\\nThe final bytecode output is encapsulated in a JSScript object:\\n\\n**JSScript (The Bytecode Container):**\\n- **`js/src/vm/JSScript.h`** (line 1787): Defines the `JSScript` class which is the primary bytecode container. JSScript inherits from `js::BaseScript` and contains:\\n  - The bytecode array (`jsbytecode* code`)\\n  - Script metadata (line numbers, source location, function information)\\n  - Scope and binding information\\n  - JIT compilation data\\n  - Debug information\\n  - Source notes for mapping bytecode back to source\\n\\nThe JSScript structure contains all necessary information for:\\n- Interpretation of bytecode\\n- JIT compilation (Ion, Baseline)\\n- Debugging and profiling\\n- Exception handling\\n- Source mapping\\n\\n## Compilation Flow Summary\\n\\n1. **Entry**: `JS::Compile()` called with source text and compile options\\n2. **Driver**: `CompileGlobalScript()` creates a `ScriptCompiler` instance\\n3. **Tokenization**: TokenStream parses source into tokens\\n4. **Parsing**: `Parser::parse()` generates ParseNode AST from tokens\\n5. **Emission**: `BytecodeEmitter` traverses AST and generates bytecode\\n6. **Stencil**: Bytecode and metadata collected in `CompilationStencil`\\n7. **Instantiation**: `InstantiateStencils()` creates final `JSScript` object\\n8. **Output**: `JSScript*` returned with executable bytecode ready for execution\\n\\n## Key Interconnections\\n\\n- **Parser \u2194 SharedContext**: Parser uses SharedContext to track scope and compilation state\\n- **ParseNode \u2194 BytecodeEmitter**: BytecodeEmitter imports and traverses Compilation Chain\\n\\n## Overview\\nThe Firefox SpiderMonkey JavaScript engine compiles source code to bytecode through a multi-stage pipeline. This document traces the complete compilation path from source text to executable bytecode.\\n\\n## Stage 1: Compilation Entry Points\\n\\nThe public API for JavaScript compilation is exposed in `js/public/CompilationAndEvaluation.h` with the `JS::Compile()` family of functions. These are the user-facing entry points that accept JavaScript source text and return compiled `JSScript*` objects containing bytecode.\\n\\nFor advanced use cases without JSContext dependency, `js/public/experimental/CompileScript.h` provides the `JS::CompileGlobalScriptToStencil()` and related functions that work with a `FrontendContext` instead of `JSContext`, enabling off-thread compilation.\\n\\n## Stage 2: Compilation Driver (Frontend)\\n\\nThe high-level compilation logic is implemented in:\\n- **`js/src/frontend/BytecodeCompiler.h`**: Declares compilation functions and compiler classes\\n- **`js/src/frontend/BytecodeCompiler.cpp`**: Implements the compilation driver\\n\\nThe key compilation function is `CompileGlobalScript()` (exported in BytecodeCompiler.h), which is the implementation of the public `JS::Compile()` API. This driver orchestrates the parsing and bytecode emission pipeline.\\n\\nThe compiler uses template classes:\\n- `SourceAwareCompiler<Unit>`: Base class for all compilers\\n- `ScriptCompiler<Unit>`: For global and eval script compilation\\n- `ModuleCompiler<Unit>`: For module compilation\\n- `StandaloneFunctionCompiler<Unit>`: For function compilation\\n\\n## Stage 3: Tokenization\\n\\nBefore parsing can begin, source text must be tokenized. This is handled by:\\n- **`js/src/frontend/TokenStream.h`**: Token stream implementation\\n- **`js/src/frontend/Token.h`**: Token type definitions\\n- **`js/src/frontend/TokenKind.h`**: Token kind enumeration\\n\\nThe token stream parses the source character-by-character and generates tokens for the parser.\\n\\n## Stage 4: Parsing (AST Generation)\\n\\nThe JavaScript parser is a recursive-descent parser that generates an Abstract Syntax Tree (AST). Each node corresponds to a grammatical production in ECMAScript.\\n\\n**Parsing Context:**\\n- **`js/src/frontend/ParseContext.h`**: Parsing context information (variable scopes, statement stacks, etc.)\\n- **`js/src/frontend/SharedContext.h`**: Shared context between parser and bytecode emitter (scope information, use strict mode, etc.)\\n\\n## Stage 5: Bytecode Emission\\n\\nOnce the AST is generated, the bytecode emitter converts it to executable bytecode. This is the core compilation stage.\\n\\n**Bytecode Emitter:**\\n- **`js/src/frontend/BytecodeEmitter.h`**: Bytecode emitter class (lines 77-150+ contain comprehensive documentation about the bytecode emission process, bytecode structures, control flow handling, and scope management)\\n- **`js/src/frontend/BytecodeEmitter.cpp`**: Complete bytecode emitter implementation (line 158 shows the constructor initialization)\\n\\nThe `BytecodeEmitter` class:\\n1. Traverses the ParseNode tree\\n2. Emits JSOp bytecode instructions (defined in `vm/Opcodes.h`)\\n3. Manages bytecode sections for prologue and main code\\n4. Handles jump patching for control flow (if/else, loops, try/catch)\\n5. Manages variable scopes and bindings\\n6. Generates source notes for debugging\\n\\n**Supporting Bytecode Components:**\\n- **`js/src/frontend/BytecodeSection.h`**: Bytecode section management\\n- **`js/src/frontend/BytecodeOffset.h`**: Bytecode offset tracking\\n- **`js/src/frontend/SourceNotes.h`/`.cpp`**: Source note generation for debugging information\\n- **`js/src/frontend/JumpList.h`**: Jump list management for forward jumps\\n- **`js/src/frontend/EmitterScope.h`**: Scope binding information during emission\\n\\n**Bytecode Output Structure:**\\n- **`js/src/frontend/Stencil.h`**: Compilation stencil structure (intermediate representation before JSScript creation)\\n- **`js/src/frontend/CompilationStencil.h`**: Extended stencil with metadata\\n\\n## Stage 6: JSScript Creation (Bytecode Output)\\n\\nThe final bytecode output is encapsulated in a JSScript object:\\n\\n**JSScript (The Bytecode Container):**\\n- **`js/src/vm/JSScript.h`** (line 1787): Defines the `JSScript` class which is the primary bytecode container. Interpretation of bytecode\\n- JIT compilation (Ion, Baseline)\\n- Debugging and profiling\\n- Exception handling\\n- Source mapping\\n\\n## Compilation Flow Summary\\n\\n1. **Entry**: `JS::Compile()` called with source text and compile options\\n2. **Driver**: `CompileGlobalScript()` creates a `ScriptCompiler` instance\\n3. **Tokenization**: TokenStream parses source into tokens\\n4. **Parsing**:
